      10             :  * This is a recursive-descent parser for the JavaScript language specified by

      12             :  * lexical and semantic feedback to disambiguate non-LL(1) structures.  It

    4409             : 
    4410             : /*
    4411             :  * Destructuring patterns can appear in two kinds of contexts:
    4412             :  *
    4413             :  * - assignment-like: assignment expressions and |for| loop heads.  In
    4414             :  *   these cases, the patterns' property value positions can be
    4415             :  *   arbitrary lvalue expressions; the destructuring is just a fancy
    4416             :  *   assignment.
    4417             :  *
    4418             :  * - binding-like: |var| and |let| declarations, functions' formal
    4419             :  *   parameter lists, |catch| clauses, and comprehension tails.  In
    4420             :  *   these cases, the patterns' property value positions must be
    4421             :  *   simple names; the destructuring defines them as new variables.
    4422             :  *
    4423             :  * In both cases, other code parses the pattern as an arbitrary
    4424             :  * primaryExpr, and then, here in checkDestructuringPattern, verify
    4425             :  * that the tree is a valid AssignmentPattern or BindingPattern.
    4426             :  *
    4427             :  * In assignment-like contexts, we parse the pattern with
    4428             :  * pc->inDestructuringDecl clear, so the lvalue expressions in the
    4429             :  * pattern are parsed normally.  primaryExpr links variable references
    4430             :  * into the appropriate use chains; creates placeholder definitions;
    4431             :  * and so on.  checkDestructuringPattern won't bind any new names and
    4432             :  * we specialize lvalues as appropriate.
    4433             :  *
    4434             :  * In declaration-like contexts, the normal variable reference
    4435             :  * processing would just be an obstruction, because we're going to
    4436             :  * define the names that appear in the property value positions as new
    4437             :  * variables anyway.  In this case, we parse the pattern with
    4438             :  * pc->inDestructuringDecl set, which directs primaryExpr to leave
    4439             :  * whatever name nodes it creates unconnected.  Then, here in
    4440             :  * checkDestructuringPattern, we require the pattern's property value
    4441             :  * positions to be simple names, and define them as appropriate to the
    4442             :  * context.
    4443             :  */
